Early morning of November 5th. A stately house in Springfield, IL.

As the first results trickle in, your old heart quickens. Hour after hour goes by, with the race on a knife’s edge -- you hold majorities in some swing states, and Conkling holds some in others. At any point, the race could tip one way or the other; but it never does. And as the results from the West start to roll in, a thought grips you. You and Conkling may not be the only ones to win states this election. Perhaps you made some moves to encourage them, that they might split Conkling’s support, but as you take in that fact -- that a couple of states have slipped out of the reach of both you and Conkling, just enough to deny the both of you a majority -- it still doesn’t feel quite real.

An urgency grips you. Harper, the humble party chairman only seeking to make a statement, now holds the key to the White House. Under normal circumstances, this would have been of no consequence; in the lead-up to the Democratic Convention, Harper indicated that his party’s aim was to put on a strong showing, and wouldn’t strike any deals with a Tildenite. But as the campaign progressed, and you demonstrated a greater openness to economic progressivism, his attitude changed. He said, during one rally, that, should his party carry any states, he would be willing to ‘work with the party that can promise the greatest commitment to the social and economic progress of the American nation.’

A deal may still be in reach. As you turn the possibility over in your mind, you feel warm, and strong, as though a mighty steam engine in your breast fueled your every movement. A quick wire to some of your trusted confidantes, who must be coming to the same conclusion you are; down the stairs, coat on, boots, hat! Wallet, and out the door! Find a carriage at this late hour that will take you to the train station!

You have quite the head-start on the President. Danville, Illinois, and Jesse Harper, and your destiny, lay just a hundred miles away.

DEAD-LOCK! PRES ELECTION WILL GO TO HOUSE FOR FIRST TIME SINCE JACKSON

As the first results trickle in, your old heart quickens. Hour after hour goes by, with the race on a knife’s edge -- you hold majorities in some swing states, and Conkling holds some in others. At any point, the race could tip one way or the other; but it never does. And as the results from the West start to roll in, a thought grips you. You and Conkling may not be the only ones to win states this election. Perhaps you made some moves to encourage them, that they might split Conkling’s support, but as you take in that fact -- that a couple of states have slipped out of the reach of both you and Conkling, just enough to deny the both of you a majority -- it still doesn’t feel quite real.

You let out a little laugh. In another world, perhaps you could strike a deal with Harper to gain his votes and win at the Electoral College, but he made it clear on the trail that he didn’t see enough of a difference between yourself and the President that he would consider such a line of action. And thus, the election will go to a contingent election in the House, where Conkling has played the long game. While his rapid additions of the six new Republican-leaning states did contribute to his party’s massive losses in the House in the midterms, the handful of representatives from those states are all Republicans, meaning that Conkling will have six more states in his corner when the contingent election comes -- enough to secure him the Presidency. He’s won.

There’s little else to do but go to bed. As you were called up by the convention under unusual circumstances, you cannot expect that you will retain any sort of leadership role in the party going forward, though the Democracy respects you for running a strong campaign. You’ll return to the quiet and calm of your private law practice, as the games of power go on without you. You’re not the kind of man prone to daydreaming, but every once and a while, at the office after a long day of tiring work, or at home as you tuck into dinner, or even in the courtroom, as you stare out the window, the case temporarily forgotten, you wonder what might have been...

CONKLING SECURES MAJORITY OVER PALMER

As the first results trickle in, your old heart quickens, but when you see Conkling’s majorities hold firm in the swing states long into the night, you allow yourself to relax. You’ve lost races before. You’ve lost battles before. You know when it’s over. You came into the race reluctantly, but willing to work hard on behalf of your party, and against the forces of corruption, but it simply wasn’t enough. Roscoe Conkling will remain president, and serve out another four years in office.

While you tried to emulate Tilden’s economic conservatism on the trail, your efforts have left your campaign at the same dead-end his own met four years ago. The times are changing, and the growing progressive wing of the party was frustrated as you consistently shot down their hopes of a fairer economy. Still, President Tilden and his faction are grateful that you stood steadfast in your conservatism, even in the face of improbable odds.

There’s little else to do but go to bed.
